B. A conceptual framework for the evolutionary origins of multicellularity. Phys. Biol. 10, 035001 (2013) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2658">41</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Rainey, P. B. &amp; Kerr, B. Cheats as first propagules: a new hypothesis for the evolution of individuality during the transition from single cells to multicellularity. Bioessays 32, 872â€“880 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2661">42</a></sup>. The field has been concerned with the evolution of germâ€“soma division of labour as the defining step in the evolution of multicellularity<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Hanschen, E. R., Shelton, D. E. &amp; Michod, R. E. in Evolutionary transitions to multicellular life: principles and mechanisms eds Nedelcu A. M., Ruiz-Trillo I. 165â€“188Springer (2015) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2665">40</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Michod, R. E. The group covariance effect and fitness trade-offs during evolutionary transitions in individuality. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 103, 9113â€“9117 (2006) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2668">43</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Michod, R. E. Evolution of individuality during the transition from unicellular to multicellular life. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 104, 8613â€“8618 (2007) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2671">44</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Rokas, A. The origins of multicellularity and the early history of the genetic toolkit for animal development. Annu. Rev. Genet. 42, 235â€“251 (2008) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2674">45</a></sup>; indeed, a recent review of animal multicellularity<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Rokas, A. The origins of multicellularity and the early history of the genetic toolkit for animal development. Annu. Rev. Genet. 42, 235â€“251 (2008) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2678">45</a></sup> does not mention the importance of cell cycle regulation and group formation. The <i>Gonium</i> genome reflects the early evolution of cell cycle regulation (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/ncomms11370#Fig3">Figs 3</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/ncomms11370#Fig4">4</a>) in undifferentiated groups, conserved and modified in differentiated <i>Volvox</i>, that is indicative of the emergence of colony level adaptations. We highlight an early and formative step, the co-option and expansion of cell cycle regulation, as important for the evolution of cooperative groups and impacting the evolution of more complicated body plans; one that may shed light on the evolutionary history of other multicellular innovations and evolutionary transitions.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec7" data-title="Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec7-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec7">Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec7-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec8">Strain and genome sequencing</h3><p>The <i>Gonium pectorale</i> strain K3-F3-4 (mating type minus, NIES-2863 from the Microbial Culture Collection at National Institute for Environmental Studies, Tsukuba, Japan, <a href="http://mcc.nies.go.jp/">http://mcc.nies.go.jp/</a>) was used for genome sequencing. <i>Gonium</i> was grown in 200â€“300â€‰ml VTAC media at 20â€‰Â°C with a 14:10â€‰h lightâ€“dark cycle using cool-white fluorescent lights (165â€“175â€‰Î¼molâ€‰m<sup>âˆ’2</sup>â€‰s<sup>âˆ’1</sup>).</p><p>For next-generation sequencing and construction of a fosmid library, total DNA was extracted. Sequencing libraries were prepared using the GS FLX Titanium Rapid Library Preparation Kit (F. Hoffmann-La Roche, Basel, Switzerland) and the TruSeq DNA Sample Prep Kit (Illumina Inc., San Diego, CA, USA) and were run on both GS FLX (F. Hoffmann-La Roche) and MiSeq (Illumina Inc.) machines. Newbler v2.6 was used to assemble the GS FLX reads. A fosmid library was constructed in-house using vector pKS300. The fosmid library (23,424 clones) and BAC library (18,048 clones, Genome Institute (CUGI), Clemson University, Clemson, SC, USA) were end-sequenced using a BigDye terminator kit v3 (Life Technologies, Carlsbad, CA, USA) analysed on automated ABI3730 capillary sequencers (Life Technologies).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec9">Evidence-based gene prediction</h3><p>Introns hint file generation was done through a two-step, iterative mapping approach using Bowtie/Tophat command lines and custom Perl scripts written by Mario Stanke as part of AUGUSTUS<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Stanke, M. &amp; Morgenstern, B. AUGUSTUS: a web server for gene prediction in eukaryotes that allows user-defined constraints. Nucleic Acids Res. 33, W465â€“W467 (2005) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2735">46</a></sup>, (available at: <a href="http://bioinf.uni-greifswald.de/bioinf/wiki/pmwiki.php?n=IncorporatingRNAseq.Tophat">http://bioinf.uni-greifswald.de/bioinf/wiki/pmwiki.php?n=IncorporatingRNAseq.Tophat</a>). AUGUSTUS version 2.6.1 was selected because its algorithm has been successfully tuned to predict genes in <i>Chlamydomonas</i> and <i>Volvox</i> genomes, which contain high GC content<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Stanke, M. &amp; Morgenstern, B. AUGUSTUS: a web server for gene prediction in eukaryotes that allows user-defined constraints. Nucleic Acids Res. 33, W465â€“W467 (2005) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2752">46</a></sup>. Reads were first mapped to the genome assembly with Tophat version 2.0.2 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Trapnell, C., Pachter, L. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. TopHat: discovering splice junctions with RNA-Seq. Bioinformatics 25, 1105â€“1111 (2009) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2756">47</a>) and the raw alignments were filtered to create an initial (intron) hints file, which was subsequently provided to AUGUSTUS during gene prediction. An exonâ€“exon junction database was generated from the initial AUGUSTUS prediction via a Perl script. The twice-mapped reads (once to the genome and once to the exonâ€“exon sequences) were then merged, filtered and a final intron hints file was created. From this, the final gene prediction with AUGUSTUS was performed.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec10">Pfam domain analysis</h3><p>Diversity and abundance of Pfam domains was determined for all published green algae genomes. Chlorophyte genomes including <i>Bathycoccus prasinos</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Moreau, H. et al. Genome Biol. 13, R74 (2012) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2770">48</a></sup>, <i>Chlamydomonas reinhardtii</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Merchant, S. S. et al. The Chlamydomonas genome reveals the evolution of key animal and plant functions. Science 318, 245â€“250 (2007) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2776">35</a></sup>, <i>Chlorella variabilis</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Blanc, G. et al. Genome Biol. 13, R39 (2012) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2789">50</a>), <i>Micromonas pusilla</i> CCMP1545 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Worden, A. Subsequent hits were counted and produced a matrix of Pfam domain diversity and abundance across green algae.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec11">Analysis of transcription-associated proteins</h3><p>Transcription-associated proteins (TAPs) include transcription factors (enhance or repress transcription) and transcription regulators (proteins which indirectly regulate transcription such as scaffold proteins, histone modification or DNA methylation). We combined three TAP classification rules for plants; PlantTFDB<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Guo, A.-Y. et al. PlantTFDB: a comprehensive plant transcription factor database. Nucleic Acids Res. 36, D966â€“D969 (2008) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2835">54</a></sup>, PlnTFDB<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="RiaÃ±o-PachÃ³n, D. M., Ruzicic, S., Dreyer, I. &amp; Mueller-Roeber, B. PlnTFDB: an integrative plant transcription factor database. BMC Bioinformatics 8, 42 (2007) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2839">55</a></sup> and PlanTAPDB<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Richardt, S., Lang, D., Reski, R., Frank, W. &amp; Rensing, S. A. PlanTAPDB, a phylogeny-based resource of plant transcription-associated proteins. Plant Physiol. 143, 1452â€“1466 (2007) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2843">56</a></sup> to make a set of classification rules for 96 TAP families. Conflicts between the three sets of rules were manually resolved using the rule that included more genes as transcription-associated proteins.</p><p>Each transcription family includes at least one, up to three, mandatory domains. Families may include up to six forbidden domains (that is, a gene <i>G</i> cannot be in family <i>F</i> if domain <i>D</i> is present); not all families have defined forbidden domains. All mandatory and forbidden domains were represented by a full-length, global, Hidden Markov Model (HMM). Available HMMs were retrieved from Pfam_ls database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Finn, R. D. et al. The Pfam protein families database. Nucleic Acids Res. 36, D281â€“D288 (2008) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2859">57</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Finn, R. D. et al. The Pfam protein families database. Nucleic Acids Res. 38, D211â€“D222 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2862">58</a></sup>. When HMMs were not available from the Pfam_ls database, custom HMMs were made using multiple sequence alignments from PlnTFDB<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="RiaÃ±o-PachÃ³n, D. M., Ruzicic, S., Dreyer, I. &amp; Mueller-Roeber, B. PlnTFDB: an integrative plant transcription factor database. BMC Bioinformatics 8, 42 (2007) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2866">55</a></sup> and the HMM was calculated using HMMER version 3.0 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Eddy, S. R. Profile hidden Markov models. Bioinformatics 14, 755â€“763 (1998) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2870">59</a>) using â€˜hmmbuildâ€™ with default parameters and â€˜hmmcalibrateâ€”seed 0â€².</p><p>Gathering cutoff thresholds (GA) for the custom HMMs were set as the lowest score of a true positive hit using a â€˜hmmscanâ€™ search against several complete Chlorophyte genomes. Chlorophyte genomes including <i>Bathycoccus prasinos</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Moreau, H. et al. Gene functionalities and genome structure in Bathycoccus prasinos reflect cellular specializations at the base of the green lineage. Genome Biol. 13, R74 (2012) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2879">48</a></sup>, <i>Chlamydomonas reinhardtii</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Merchant, S. Science 318, 245â€“250 (2007) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2885">35</a></sup>, <i>Chlorella variabilis</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Blanc, G. et al. The Chlorella variabilis NC64A genome reveals adaptation to photosymbiosis, coevolution with viruses, and cryptic sex. Plant Cell 22, 2943â€“2955 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2891">49</a></sup>, <i>Coccomyxa subellipsoidea</i> C-169 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Blanc, G. et al. Z. et al. Green evolution and dynamic adaptations revealed by genomes of the marine Picoeukaryotes Micromonas. Science 324, 268â€“272 (2009) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2904">51</a>), <i>Micromonas pusilla</i> RCC299 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Worden, A. Z. et al. Green evolution and dynamic adaptations revealed by genomes of the marine Picoeukaryotes Micromonas. Science 324, 268â€“272 (2009) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2910">51</a>), <i>Ostreococcus tauri</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Derelle, E. et al. The tiny eukaryote Ostreococcus provides genomic insights into the paradox of plankton speciation. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 104, 7705â€“7710 (2007) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2923">53</a></sup>, <i>Ostreococcus</i> sp. RCC809 (available on the DOE Phytozome website, version 10.1) and <i>Volvox carteri</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Prochnik, S. E. et al. Genomic analysis of organismal complexity in the multicellular green alga Volvox carteri. Science 329, 223â€“226 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2932">17</a></sup> were searched using â€˜hmmscanâ€™ to search the library of 103 domains against the predicted protein sequences. Analyses were replicated with both <i>Volvox</i> version 1 and version 2; however, as results were not qualitatively different, results from version 1 are provided (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ncomms11370#MOESM570">Supplementary Fig. 3</a>). Subsequent hits were classified into a TAP family. Conflicts between multiple TAP families were resolved by assigning the gene to the TAP family with the highest score (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ncomms11370#MOESM570">Supplementary Table 1</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec12">Construction of protein families</h3><p>Protein families were created using OrthoMCL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Li, L., Stoeckert, C. J. &amp; Roos, D. S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 13, 2178â€“2189 (2003) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2955">60</a></sup> with a variety of inflation values ranging from 1.2 to 4.0 in steps of 0.1 (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ncomms11370#MOESM570">Supplementary Figs 16â€“17</a>). This analysis was performed using Chlorophyte genomes available on the DOE JGI Phytozome website, version 10.1 including <i>Bathycoccus prasinos</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Moreau, H. et al. Gene functionalities and genome structure in Bathycoccus prasinos reflect cellular specializations at the base of the green lineage. Genome Biol. 13, R74 (2012) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2964">48</a></sup>, <i>Chlamydomonas reinhardtii</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Merchant, S. S. et al. The Chlamydomonas genome reveals the evolution of key animal and plant functions. Science 318, 245â€“250 (2007) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2970">35</a></sup>, <i>Chlorella variabilis</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Blanc, G. et al. The Chlorella variabilis NC64A genome reveals adaptation to photosymbiosis, coevolution with viruses, and cryptic sex. Plant Cell 22, 2943â€“2955 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2977">49</a></sup>, <i>Coccomyxa subellipsoidea</i> C-169 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Blanc, G. et al. The genome of the polar eukaryotic microalga Coccomyxa subellipsoidea reveals traits of cold adaptation. Genome Biol. 13, R39 (2012) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2983">50</a>), <i>Micromonas pusilla</i> CCMP1545 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Worden, A. Z. et al. Green evolution and dynamic adaptations revealed by genomes of the marine Picoeukaryotes Micromonas. Science 324, 268â€“272 (2009) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2989">51</a>), <i>Micromonas pusilla</i> RCC299 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Worden, A. Z. et al. Green evolution and dynamic adaptations revealed by genomes of the marine Picoeukaryotes Micromonas. Science 324, 268â€“272 (2009) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d3334e2996">51</a>), <i>Ostreococcus tauri</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Derelle, E. et al. Genome analysis of the smallest free-living eukaryote Ostreococcus tauri unveils many unique features. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 103, 11647â€“11652 (2006) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3002">52</a></sup>, <i>Ostreococcus lucimarinus</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Palenik, B. et al. The tiny eukaryote Ostreococcus provides genomic insights into the paradox of plankton speciation. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 104, 7705â€“7710 (2007) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3008">53</a></sup>, <i>Ostreococcus</i> sp. RCC809 (available on the DOE Joint Genome Institute website) and <i>Volvox carteri</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Prochnik, S. E. et al. Genomic analysis of organismal complexity in the multicellular green alga Volvox carteri. Science 329, 223â€“226 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3018">17</a></sup>. This analysis was repeated for both <i>Volvox</i> version 1 and <i>Volvox</i> version 2. The inflation value of 1.9 was used for both analyses for consistency and was chosen to have relatively large, coarser grained clusters that were robust to higher inflation values (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ncomms11370#MOESM570">Supplementary Figs 16â€“19</a>). To avoid bias introduced by not including all genes for each species, genes not assigned to a gene family (singletons) were assigned to single gene families and included in all subsequent phylogenetic gene family analyses.</p><p>A species tree was calculated by extracting OrthoMCL gene families containing only one copy in each species, for a total of 1,457 genes. The OrthoMCL run with an inflation value of 1.5 was chosen to use larger, coarser grained clusters, thus increasing the likelihood of capturing true 1:1:1 orthologues. This species tree included <i>Volvox carteri</i> version 2. These genes were independently aligned using Muscle version 3.8.31 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Edgar, R. C. MUSCLE: multiple sequence alignment with high accuracy and high throughput. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, 1792â€“1797 (2004) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3036">61</a>) and concatenated. A phylogenetic tree was produced using RAxML version 8.0.20 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Stamatakis, A. RAxML version 8: a tool for phylogenetic analysis and post-analysis of large phylogenies. Bioinformatics 30, 1312â€“1313 (2014) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3039">62</a>) using the Protein Gamma model with automatic model selection on a per gene basis via partitions for each protein. A rapid bootstrapping analysis to search for the best-scoring ML tree was run with 100 bootstraps. The resulting species tree is consistent with previous results<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Herron, M. D. &amp; Michod, R. E. Evolution of complexity in the volvocine algae: transitions in individuality through Darwinâ€™s eye. Evolution 62, 436â€“451 (2008) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3043">16</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Worden, A. Z. et al. Green evolution and dynamic adaptations revealed by genomes of the marine Picoeukaryotes Micromonas. Science 324, 268â€“272 (2009) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3046">51</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Worden, A. Z. &amp; Not, F. in Microbial Ecology Of the Oceans ed. Kirchman D. 159â€“205Wiley (2008) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3049">63</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Nozaki, H. Origin and evolution of the genera Pleodorina and Volvox (Volvocales). Biologia 58, 425â€“431 (2003) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3052">64</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Leliaert, F. et al. Phylogeny and molecular evolution of the green algae. CRC Crit. Rev. Plant Sci. 31, 1â€“46 (2012) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3055">65</a></sup> and had 100 bootstrap support at every node (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ncomms11370#MOESM570">Supplementary Fig. 20</a>). This result is also consistent with numerous morphological characteristics supporting a closer relationship of <i>Gonium</i> and <i>Volvox</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Nozaki, H. &amp; Itoh, M. Phylogenetic relationships within the colonial Volvocales (Chlorophyta) inferred from cladistic analysis based on morphological data. J. Phycol. 30, 353â€“365 (1994) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3068">66</a></sup>.</p><p>Gene family evolution within the volvocine algae was analysed using Count version 10.04 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="CsurÃ¶s, M. Count: evolutionary analysis of phylogenetic profiles with parsimony and likelihood. Bioinformatics 26, 1910â€“1912 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3074">67</a>) to perform several parsimony analyses including symmetric Wagner parsimony (each gene family may be gained or expanded multiple times and the gain penalty is equal to the loss penalty) and asymmetric Wagner parsimony (each gene family may be gained or expanded multiple times and the gain penalty is two times higher than the loss penalty). This analysis was repeated for both <i>Volvox</i> version 1 and version 2 genomes (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ncomms11370#MOESM570">Supplementary Tables 5â€“8</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">dN/dS analysis</h3><p>During our OrthoMCL construction of protein gene families, we identified 6,154 clusters with exactly one copy in <i>Chlamydomonas</i> (version 5.3), <i>Gonium</i> and <i>Volvox</i> (version 2). The number of genes from other unicellular (non-<i>Chlamydomonas</i>) Chlorophyte species was ignored. This criteria is relatively strict as it does not include any genes with a duplicate in any species (copy number greater than one in any species) or any genes which are not essential (no copy present in any species) resulting in 1:1:1 orthologues. Given the relatively high gene duplication rates in volvocine algae (data not shown), these strict criteria support an interpretation of 1:1:1 orthology. Genome-wide pairwise comparisons of dN, dS and dN/dS were calculated (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ncomms11370#MOESM570">Supplementary Fig. 21</a>; <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ncomms11370#MOESM570">Supplementary Table 11</a>) using PAML and codeml (ML analysis<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Yang, Z. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol. Biol. Evol. 24, 1586â€“1591 (2007) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3111">68</a></sup>) based on nucleotide translation based alignments (proteins were aligned using MUSCLE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Edgar, R. C. MUSCLE: multiple sequence alignment with high accuracy and high throughput. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, 1792â€“1797 (2004) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3115">61</a></sup>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">Prediction of lineage-specific genes</h3><p>The phylostratigraphy method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Domazet-Loso, T., Brajkovic, J. &amp; Tautz, D. A phylostratigraphy approach to uncover the genomic history of major adaptations in metazoan lineages. Trends Genet. 23, 533â€“539 (2007) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3127">20</a></sup> assumes Dolloâ€™s parsimony (that is, it is more likely that a gene observed in two distant clades was present in the common ancestor and multiple independent gains are not possible). This provides an entry point for testing evolutionary hypotheses related to the age of genes and to quantify how much gene-level innovation has occurred along each phylogenetic branch. Old genes are classified in low phylostrata (present in distant species, PS1â€“PS7) and young genes are classified in higher phylostrata (for example, genus- or species-specific genes, PS8â€“PS9). The resolution of each phylostratum strictly depends on the availability of reliable outgroups (the availability of reliable genomic outgroups is relatively low in Chlorophyte algae). The phylogenetic classes were defined from those in each NCBI Taxonomy entry for <i>Chlamydomonas</i>, <i>Gonium</i> and <i>Volvox</i>, resulting in nine expected phylostrata for each species. All proteins were subjected to a BLASTP search with an <i>E</i>-value threshold of 0.001 against the NCBI nr database. Placement in phylostrata was derived from the taxonomic information of these hits for each protein, using the most distant hit, and following Dolloâ€™s parsimony.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Phylogenetic analyses</h3><p>Unless otherwise stated, all phylogenetic analyses were performed using a custom pipeline of SATe version 2.2.7 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Liu, K., Raghavan, S., Nelesen, S., Linder, C. R. &amp; Warnow, T. Rapid and accurate large-scale coestimation of sequence alignments and phylogenetic trees. Science 324, 1561â€“1564 (2009) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3150">69</a>) coupled with RAxML version 8 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Stamatakis, A. RAxML version 8: a tool for phylogenetic analysis and post-analysis of large phylogenies. Bioinformatics 30, 1312â€“1313 (2014) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3153">62</a>). Full gene protein sequences were passed to SATe using a FASTTREE tree estimation with a RAxML search after tree formation with a maximum limit of 10 iterations and the â€˜longestâ€™ decomposition strategy. Bootstraps were made on the SATe output alignment and tree using RAxML with automatic model selection, a rapid hill climbing algorithm (âˆ’f d) and 100 bootstrap partitions. Bipartition information (âˆ’f a) was obtained using the SATe output tree and RAxML bootstraps.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16"><i>Chlamydomonas</i> strains culture conditions</h3><p>Wild-type <i>Chlamydomonas reinhardtii</i> 6145 and 21gr, and <i>HA-CrRB</i> (<i>HA-MAT3::mat3â€“4</i>, here referred to as <i>HA-CrRB::rb</i>), <i>mat3â€“4</i> (here referred to as <i>rb</i>), and <i>dp1</i> have been previously described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Umen, J. G. &amp; Goodenough, U. W. Control of cell division by a retinoblastoma protein homolog in Chlamydomonas. Genes Dev. 15, 1652â€“1661 (2001) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3190">9</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Fang, S.-C., de los Reyes, C. &amp; Umen, J. G. Cell size checkpoint control by the retinoblastoma tumor suppressor pathway. PLoS Genet. 2, e167 (2006) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3193">10</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3196">11</a></sup>. Briefly, wild-type strains 6145 (MTâˆ’) and 21gr (MT+) are mating pairs that have been back crossed to eliminate the <i>y1</i> mutation in 6145 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Fang, S.-C., de los Reyes, C. &amp; Umen, J. G. Cell size checkpoint control by the retinoblastoma tumor suppressor pathway. PLoS Genet. 2, e167 (2006) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3202">10</a>). The <i>RB</i> knockout strain has been previously characterized as a null allele, and the knockout mutation is the <i>rb</i> allele<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Umen, J. G. &amp; Goodenough, U. W. Control of cell division by a retinoblastoma protein homolog in Chlamydomonas. Genes Dev. 15, 1652â€“1661 (2001) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3213">9</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3216">11</a></sup>. The <i>rb</i> mutation can be complemented by a amino (N)-terminally tagged version of the gene that behaves identical to wild type. Previously, a knockout mutation in the <i>Chlamydomonas DP1</i> gene, <i>dp1</i>, was identified and characterized<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Fang, S.-C., de los Reyes, C. &amp; Umen, J. G. Cell size checkpoint control by the retinoblastoma tumor suppressor pathway. PLoS Genet. 2, e167 (2006) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3229">10</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3232">11</a></sup>. All the strains were maintained on TAP plates. For phenotype analysis, the strains were grown in high salt media (HSM) synchronously under 14â€‰h of 150â€‰Î¼E of light, samples were fixed hourly and examined by light microscopy<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Fang, S.-C., de los Reyes, C. &amp; Umen, J. G. Cell size checkpoint control by the retinoblastoma tumor suppressor pathway. PLoS Genet. 2, e167 (2006) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3237">10</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3240">11</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17">Cloning of <i>Gonium pectorale RB</i> and transformation into <i>rb</i></h3><p>A 3X haemagluttin (HA) tagged copy of the <i>Gonium pectorale RB</i> gene was cloned using InFusion Cloning (Clontech) to be driven by the <i>Chlamydomonas RB</i> promoter and terminator that includes a <i>AphVIII</i> selectable marker for <i>Chlamydomonas</i> transformation (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/ncomms11370#Fig4">Fig. 4</a>, (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3273">11</a>)). <i>Gonium pectorale</i> genomic DNA from K4F3 was used as a template and the genomic region of <i>RB</i> was amplified without its ATG start codon using the primers 5â€²-CAGATTACGCTACTAGATCTGCCGAAGCTGAACGTTTTACTGCG-3â€², and 5â€²-CTCCGGCCGCGGTGCCTAATTTGCGCCGTACCGCCGGA-3â€². These primers overlap with the 3X HA tag and 3â€² terminator from the previously created HA-CrRB transformation clone that complements the <i>rb</i> mutation<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3286">11</a></sup>. The HA-CrRB plasmid was amplified by inverse PCR with 5â€²-TCTAGTAGCGTAATCTGGAACGTCATATGGATAGG-3â€² and 5â€²-GCACCGCGGCCGGAGGT-3â€² primers. PCR products were gel purified with a QiaQuick gel extraction kit (Qiagen). Purified PCR fragments were fused by InFusion (Clontech) cloning based on overlaps in the amplified sequences and transformed into chemically competent DH5-apha cells, after which the clone was confirmed by sequencing.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec18">Transformation of <i>Chlamydomonas reinhardtii</i></h3><p>The <i>rb</i> strain was transformed with glass beads<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3305">11</a></sup>, with the <i>HA-GpRB</i> clone (above) and as a control with <i>HA-CrRB</i> and pSI103 (<i>AphVIII</i> selectable marker only) and selected on TAP plates supplemented with 20â€‰Î¼gâ€‰ml<sup>âˆ’1</sup> paromycin<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3321">11</a></sup>. Candidate strains were screened by growth morphology<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Fang, S.-C., de los Reyes, C. &amp; Umen, J. G. Cell size checkpoint control by the retinoblastoma tumor suppressor pathway. PLoS Genet. 2, e167 (2006) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3325">10</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3328">11</a></sup>, and then screened for expression by immunoblotting with an anti-HA antibody (Roche 3F10, high affinity<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3332">11</a></sup>). Four independent strains expressing the <i>HA-GpRB</i>, and five independent strains expressing <i>HA-CrRB</i> were created. Control complementation of the <i>rb</i> mutation with <i>HA-CrRB</i> occurred at rates similar to previous results<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3349">11</a></sup>. The presence of the <i>rb</i> mutation was confirmed by replica plating on TAP plates supplemented with 10â€‰Î¼gâ€‰ml<sup>âˆ’1</sup> emetine<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Umen, J. G. &amp; Goodenough, U. W. Control of cell division by a retinoblastoma protein homolog in Chlamydomonas. Genes Dev. 15, 1652â€“1661 (2001) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3358">9</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3361">11</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19">Genetic analysis of <i>HA-GpRB</i>-expressing strains</h3><p>Two lines expressing <i>HA-GpRB</i> were crossed to a <i>dp1</i> null mutation<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Fang, S.-C., de los Reyes, C. &amp; Umen, J. G. Cell size checkpoint control by the retinoblastoma tumor suppressor pathway. PLoS Genet. 2, e167 (2006) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3383">10</a></sup>. Because both the <i>HA-GpRB</i> and <i>dp1</i> mutations are linked to <i>AphVIII,</i> single tetrads were dissected. <i>HA-GpRB</i> was genotyped with primers in the 3XHA tag 5â€²-AGTGCTAACAGCATGTCTAGTTAC-3â€², and in the 5â€² portion of <i>GpRB</i> 5â€²-TGCGAACAACCGCTGCAGACCTTC-3â€². The <i>dp1</i> mutation was genotyped as previously described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Fang, S.-C., de los Reyes, C. &amp; Umen, J. G. Cell size checkpoint control by the retinoblastoma tumor suppressor pathway. PLoS Genet. 2, e167 (2006) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3406">10</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20">Immunoblotting <i>HA-GpRB</i> and <i>HA-CrRB</i> strains complementing <i>rb</i></h3><p>Whole-cell lysates from strains were prepared, separated and immunoblotted<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3427">11</a></sup>. Briefly, the anti-HA antibody used for detection of <i>HA-GpRB</i> and <i>HA-CrRB</i> was an anti-HA high affinity monoclonal antibody (clone 3F10, Roche) and anti-alpha-tubulin monoclonal antibody (Sigma), as previously described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3437">11</a></sup>. The expression levels of <i>RB</i> in <i>HA-CrRB</i> strains have been previously shown to be similar to wild-type <i>Chlamydomonas</i> expression levels<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3451">11</a></sup>. The expression levels of <i>RB</i> in <i>HA-GpRB</i> are similar, if not slightly below, the expression levels of <i>HA-CrRB</i>, suggesting that overexpression of <i>RB</i> is not causing the observed colonial phenotype, but rather modification to the <i>Gonium RB</i> gene.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">Measurement of cell or colony size distribution</h3><p>The size of cells and groups of cells was measured with a Moxi Z automated cell sizer/counter using type â€˜Sâ€™ cassettes (ORFLO Technologies). Sizing is based on the Coulter principle used previously with <i>Chlamydomonas reinhardtii</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Fang, S.-C., de los Reyes, C. &amp; Umen, J. G. Cell size checkpoint control by the retinoblastoma tumor suppressor pathway. PLoS Genet. 2, e167 (2006) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3481">10</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Olson, B. J. S. C. et al. Regulation of the Chlamydomonas cell cycle by a stable, chromatin-associated retinoblastoma tumor suppressor complex. Plant Cell 22, 3331â€“3347 (2010) ." href="/articles/ncomms11370#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d3334e3484">11</a></sup>.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec22" data-title="Additional information"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec22-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec22">Additional information</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec22-content"><p><b>Accession codes:</b> This Whole Genome Shotgun project has been deposited at DDBJ/ENA/GenBank under the accession <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/?term=LSYV00000000">LSYV00000000</a>.                    data-track-label="link:The state of algal genome quality and diversity"
                   href="https://doi.org/10.1016/j.algal.2020.101968"
                   id="title-link-4">
                  The state of algal genome quality and diversity
                </a>
              </h3>

                  <li><span
